<p><b>Brooklyn</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ʊ/ short 'oo' in 'foot'">ʊ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɪ/ or /ə/ 'e' in 'roses'">ᵻ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is the most populous of New York City's five boroughs, with a Census-estimated 2,636,735 residents in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-BrooklynQuickFacts_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BrooklynQuickFacts-1">[1]</a></sup> It is geographically adjacent to the borough of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> at the southwestern end of <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>. Since 1896, Brooklyn has had the same boundaries as <b>Kings County</b>, the most populous <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county</a> in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_populous_counties_in_the_United_States" title="List of the most populous counties in the United States">second-most densely populated county</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">county of New York</a> (which is coextensive with the borough of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>With a land area of 71 square miles (180&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) and water area of 26 square miles (67&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), Kings County is New York's fourth-smallest county by land area and third-smallest by total area, though it is the second-largest among the city's five boroughs.<sup id="cite_ref-GR1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-4">[4]</a></sup> Today, if each of the five boroughs were a separate city, Brooklyn would rank as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">third-most populous city in the U.S.</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>.</p>
<p>Brooklyn was an independent incorporated city (and previously an authorized village and town within the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="New York State Constitution">New York State Constitution</a>) until January 1, 1898 when, after a long <a href="/wiki/City_of_Greater_New_York" title="City of Greater New York">political campaign and public relations battle</a> during the 1890s, according to the new Municipal Charter of "Greater New York", Brooklyn was consolidated with the other cities, boroughs, and counties to form the modern "City of New York" surrounding the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Bay" title="New York Bay">Upper New York Bay</a> with five constituent boroughs. The borough continues, however, to maintain a <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brooklyn" title="Culture of Brooklyn">distinct culture</a>. Many <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brooklyn_neighborhoods" title="List of Brooklyn neighborhoods">Brooklyn neighborhoods</a> are <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_enclave" title="Ethnic enclave">ethnic enclaves</a>. Brooklyn's official motto, displayed on the Borough <a href="/wiki/Seal_(device)" class="mw-redirect" title="Seal (device)">seal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flags_of_New_York_City%27s_boroughs#Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Flags of New York City's boroughs">flag</a>, is <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl"><i>Eendraght Maeckt Maght</i></span> which translates from early modern <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> as "<a href="/wiki/Unity_makes_strength" title="Unity makes strength">Unity makes strength</a>".</p>
<p>In the first decades of the <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a> Brooklyn has experienced a <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">renaissance</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Avant_garde" class="mw-redirect" title="Avant garde">avant garde</a> destination for <a href="/wiki/Hipster_(contemporary_subculture)" title="Hipster (contemporary subculture)">hipsters</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> with concomitant <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a>, dramatic <a href="/wiki/House_price" class="mw-redirect" title="House price">house price</a> increases, and a decrease in <a href="/wiki/Housing_affordability" class="mw-redirect" title="Housing affordability">housing affordability</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Since 2010 it has evolved into a thriving hub of <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurship</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high technology</a> <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startup firms</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BrooklynDesignHub_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BrooklynDesignHub-8">[8]</a></sup> and of <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_art" title="Postmodern art">postmodern art</a><sup id="cite_ref-BrooklynArt1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BrooklynArt1-9">[9]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Design" title="Design">design</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BrooklynDesignHub_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BrooklynDesignHub-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" border="1" style="float:right; text-align:right; font-size:85%; margin:1em;">

<div class="mw-stack" style="box-sizing: border-box; float:right;">
<div style="overflow: hidden; margin: 1px;">
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg/250px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg" width="250" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg/375px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg/500px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="608" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_Hooker%27s_Map_of_the_Village_of_Brooklyn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brooklyn Museum - Hooker's Map of the Village of Brooklyn</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Brooklyn" title="Timeline of Brooklyn">Timeline of Brooklyn</a></div>
<p>The history of <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European</a> settlement in Brooklyn spans more than 350 years. The settlement began in the 17th century as the small <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Dutch colonization of the Americas">Dutch-founded</a> town of "Breuckelen" on the <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">East River</a> shore of <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, grew to be a sizable city in the 19th century, and was consolidated in 1898 with New York City (then confined to <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">the Bronx</a>), the remaining rural areas of Kings County, and the largely rural areas of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a>, to form the modern City of New York.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Six_Dutch_towns">Six Dutch towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Six Dutch towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> were the first Europeans to settle Long Island's western edge, which was then largely inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Lenape</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> people who are often referred to in contemporary colonial documents by a variation of the place name "<a href="/wiki/Canarsie" class="mw-redirect" title="Canarsie">Canarsie</a>". The "Breuckelen" settlement, named after <a href="/wiki/Breukelen" title="Breukelen">Breukelen</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, was part of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> lost little time in chartering the six original parishes (listed here first by their later, more common English names):<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gravesend,_Brooklyn" title="Gravesend, Brooklyn">Gravesend</a>: in 1645, settled under Dutch patent by <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> followers of the <a href="/wiki/Anabaptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anabaptist">Anabaptist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Deborah_Moody" class="mw-redirect" title="Lady Deborah Moody">Lady Deborah Moody</a>, possibly after <a href="/wiki/Gravesend" title="Gravesend">Gravesend</a>, England, or <a href="/wiki/%27s-Gravenzande" title="'s-Gravenzande">'s-Gravenzande</a>, Netherlands</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Heights,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Heights, Brooklyn">Brooklyn Heights</a>: as "Breuckelen" in 1646, after the town now spelled "<a href="/wiki/Breukelen" title="Breukelen">Breukelen</a>", <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flatlands,_Brooklyn" title="Flatlands, Brooklyn">Flatlands</a>: as "New <a href="/wiki/Amersfoort" title="Amersfoort">Amersfoort</a>" in 1647</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flatbush,_Brooklyn" title="Flatbush, Brooklyn">Flatbush</a>: as "<a href="/wiki/Midwood,_Brooklyn" title="Midwood, Brooklyn">Midwout</a>" in 1652</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Utrecht,_Brooklyn" title="New Utrecht, Brooklyn">New Utrecht</a>: in 1657, after the city of <a href="/wiki/Utrecht_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Utrecht (city)">Utrecht</a>, Netherlands</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bushwick,_Brooklyn" title="Bushwick, Brooklyn">Bushwick</a>: as "Boswijck" in 1661</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dining_table_in_Brooklyn,_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Dining_table_in_Brooklyn%2C_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG/250px-Dining_table_in_Brooklyn%2C_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Dining_table_in_Brooklyn%2C_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG/375px-Dining_table_in_Brooklyn%2C_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Dining_table_in_Brooklyn%2C_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG/500px-Dining_table_in_Brooklyn%2C_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dining_table_in_Brooklyn,_c._1664_IMG_3837.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A typical dining table in the Dutch village of Brooklyn, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1664</span>, from <a href="/wiki/The_Brooklyn_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="The Brooklyn Museum">The Brooklyn Museum</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The colony's capital, <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> across the East River, obtained its charter later than the village of Brooklyn did, in 1653. The neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Marine_Park" title="Marine Park">Marine Park</a> was home to North America's first tidal mill. It was built by the Dutch, and the foundation can be seen today. However, the area was not formally settled as a town. Many incidents and documents relating to this period are in <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Furman" title="Gabriel Furman">Gabriel Furman</a>'s early (1824) compilation.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Six_townships_in_an_English_province">Six townships in an English province</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Six townships in an English province">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BrooklynMap1766.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/BrooklynMap1766.jpg/250px-BrooklynMap1766.jpg" width="250" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/BrooklynMap1766.jpg/375px-BrooklynMap1766.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/BrooklynMap1766.jpg/500px-BrooklynMap1766.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1882" data-file-height="1629" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BrooklynMap1766.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Village of Brooklyn and environs, 1766</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>What is today Brooklyn left Dutch hands after the final <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> conquest of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a> in 1664, a prelude to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo%E2%80%93Dutch_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Anglo–Dutch War">Second Anglo–Dutch War</a>. New Netherland was taken in a naval action, and the conquerors renamed their prize in honor of the overall English naval commander, <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James, Duke of York</a>, brother of the then monarch <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">King Charles II of England</a> and future king himself as <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">King James II of England and James VII of Scotland</a>; Brooklyn became a part of the new English and later British colony, the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">Province of New York</a>.</p>
<p>The English reorganized the six old Dutch towns on southwestern Long Island as <i>Kings County</i> on November 1, 1683,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> one of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York#Counties" title="Province of New York">"original twelve counties"</a> then established in New York Province. This tract of land was recognized as a political entity for the first time, and the municipal groundwork was laid for a later expansive idea of Brooklyn identity.</p>
<p>Lacking the <a href="/wiki/Patroon" title="Patroon">patroon</a> and tenant farmer system established along the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley" title="Hudson Valley">Hudson River Valley</a>, this <a href="/wiki/Agricultural" class="mw-redirect" title="Agricultural">agricultural</a> county unusually came to have one of the highest percentages of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_colonial_United_States" title="Slavery in the colonial United States">slavery</a> among the population in the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">"Original Thirteen Colonies"</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> eastern coast of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolutionary_War">Revolutionary War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Revolutionary War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Long_Island" title="Battle of Long Island">Battle of Long Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Jersey_campaign" title="New York and New Jersey campaign">New York and New Jersey campaign</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg/250px-Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg" width="250" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg/375px-Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg/500px-Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="565" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle-of-Long-Island-Map-sml.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Long_Island" title="Battle of Long Island">Battle of Long Island</a> was fought across Kings County.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On August 27, 1776 was fought the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Long_Island" title="Battle of Long Island">Battle of Long Island</a> (also known as the 'Battle of Brooklyn'), the first major engagement fought in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> after independence was declared, and the largest of the entire conflict. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">British</a> troops forced <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a> troops under <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> off the heights near the modern sites of <a href="/wiki/Green-Wood_Cemetery" title="Green-Wood Cemetery">Green-Wood Cemetery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Park_(Brooklyn)" title="Prospect Park (Brooklyn)">Prospect Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Army_Plaza" title="Grand Army Plaza">Grand Army Plaza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Washington, viewing <a href="/wiki/Old_Stone_House_(Brooklyn)" title="Old Stone House (Brooklyn)">particularly fierce fighting</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Gowanus_Canal" title="Gowanus Canal">Gowanus Creek</a> from atop a hill near the west end of present-day <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Avenue_(Brooklyn)" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Avenue (Brooklyn)">Atlantic Avenue</a>, was famously reported to have emotionally exclaimed: "What brave men I must this day lose!".<sup id="cite_ref-McCullough.2C_David_2005_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCullough.2C_David_2005-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">fortified</a> American positions at <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Heights,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Heights, Brooklyn">Brooklyn Heights</a> consequently became untenable and were evacuated a few days later, leaving the British in control of <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York Harbor</a>. While Washington's defeat on the battlefield cast early doubts on his ability as the commander, the <a href="/wiki/Tactical_withdrawal" class="mw-redirect" title="Tactical withdrawal">tactical withdrawal</a> of all his troops and supplies across the <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">East River</a> in a single night is now seen by historians as one of his most brilliant triumphs.<sup id="cite_ref-McCullough.2C_David_2005_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCullough.2C_David_2005-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British controlled the surrounding region for the duration of the war, as New York City was soon occupied and became their military and political base of operations in <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">North America</a> for the remainder of the conflict. The British generally enjoyed a dominant <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalist</a> sentiment from the residents in Kings County who did not evacuate, though the region was also the center of the fledgling—and largely successful—<a href="/wiki/Intelligence_in_the_American_Revolutionary_War" title="Intelligence in the American Revolutionary War">American intelligence network</a>, headed by Washington himself.</p>
<p>The British set up a system of notorious <a href="/wiki/Prison_Ship_Martyrs%27_Monument" title="Prison Ship Martyrs' Monument">prison ships</a> off the coast of Brooklyn in <a href="/wiki/Wallabout_Bay" title="Wallabout Bay">Wallabout Bay</a>, where more American <a href="/wiki/Patriot_(American_Revolution)" title="Patriot (American Revolution)">patriots</a> died of intentional neglect than died in combat on all the battlefields of the American Revolutionary War, combined. One result of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> in 1783 was the <a href="/wiki/Evacuation_Day_(New_York)" title="Evacuation Day (New York)">evacuation of the British from New York City</a>, celebrated by residents into the 20th century.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-colonial_era">Post-colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Urbanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/250px-Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="250" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/375px-Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/500px-Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4001" data-file-height="3204" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Francis_Guy_-_Winter_Scene_in_Brooklyn_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A preindustrial <i>Winter Scene in Brooklyn</i>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1819–20</span>, by Francis Guy (<a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first half of the 19th century saw the beginning of the development of urban areas on the economically strategic East River shore of Kings County, facing the adolescent City of New York confined to Manhattan Island. The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Naval_Shipyard" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Naval Shipyard">New York Navy Yard</a> operated in <a href="/wiki/Wallabout_Bay" title="Wallabout Bay">Wallabout Bay</a> (border between Brooklyn and Williamsburgh) for the entire 19th century and two-thirds of the 20th century.</p>
<p>The first center of <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> sprang up in the Town of Brooklyn, directly across from <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>, which saw the incorporation of the Village of Brooklyn in 1816. Reliable steam <a href="/wiki/List_of_ferries_across_the_East_River" title="List of ferries across the East River">ferry service</a> across the East River to <a href="/wiki/Fulton_Ferry,_Brooklyn" title="Fulton Ferry, Brooklyn">Fulton Landing</a> converted <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Heights,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Heights, Brooklyn">Brooklyn Heights</a> into a <a href="/wiki/Commuter_town" title="Commuter town">commuter town</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a>. Ferry Road to Jamaica Pass became <a href="/wiki/Fulton_Street_(Brooklyn)" title="Fulton Street (Brooklyn)">Fulton Street</a> to <a href="/wiki/East_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="East New York">East New York</a>. Town and Village were combined to form the first, kernel incarnation of the City of Brooklyn in 1834.</p>
<p>In parallel development, the Town of Bushwick, a little farther up the river, saw the incorporation of the Village of <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Brooklyn" title="Williamsburg, Brooklyn">Williamsburgh</a> in 1827, which separated as the Town of Williamsburgh in 1840 and formed the short-lived City of Williamsburgh in 1851. <a href="/wiki/Industrial_deconcentration" title="Industrial deconcentration">Industrial deconcentration</a> in mid-century was bringing shipbuilding and other manufacturing to the northern part of the county. Each of the two cities and six towns in Kings County remained independent municipalities, and purposely created non-aligning street grids with different naming systems.</p>
<p>However, the East River shore was growing too fast for the three-year-old infant City of Williamsburgh; it, along with its Town of <a href="/wiki/Bushwick,_Brooklyn" title="Bushwick, Brooklyn">Bushwick</a> hinterland, was subsumed within a greater City of Brooklyn in 1854.</p>
<p>By 1841, with the appearance of the <i><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Eagle" title="Brooklyn Eagle">The Brooklyn Eagle, and Kings County Democrat</a></i> published by Alfred G. Stevens, the growing city across the East River from Manhattan was producing its own prominent newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It later became the most popular and highest circulation afternoon paper in America. The publisher changed to L. Van Anden on April 19, 1842,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and the paper was renamed <i>The Brooklyn Daily Eagle and Kings County Democrat</i> on June 1, 1846.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> On May 14, 1849 the name was shortened to <i>The Brooklyn Daily Eagle</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> on September 5, 1938 it was further shortened to <i>Brooklyn Eagle</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The establishment of the paper in the 1840s helped develop a separate identity for Brooklynites over the next century. The borough's soon-to-be-famous <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> baseball team, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a>, also assisted with this. Both major institutions were lost in the 1950s: the paper closed in 1955 after unsuccessful attempts at a sale following a reporters' strike, and the baseball team decamped for Los Angeles in a realignment of <a href="/wiki/Major_league_baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="Major league baseball">major league baseball</a> in 1957.</p>
<p>Agitation against Southern slavery was stronger in Brooklyn than in New York, and under Republican leadership the city was fervent in the Union cause in the <a href="/wiki/US_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="US Civil War">Civil War</a>. After the war the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ward_Beecher_Monument" title="Henry Ward Beecher Monument">Henry Ward Beecher Monument</a> was built downtown to honor a famous local <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">abolitionist</a>. A great victory arch was built at what was then the south end of town to celebrate the armed forces; this place is now called <a href="/wiki/Grand_Army_Plaza" title="Grand Army Plaza">Grand Army Plaza</a>.</p>
<p>The city had a population of 25,000 in 1834, but the police department only comprised 12 men on the day shift and another 12 at night. Every time a rash of burglaries broke out, officials blamed burglars coming in from New York City. Finally in 1855, a modern police force was created, employing 150 men. Voters complained of inadequate protection and excessive costs. In 1857 the state legislature merged the Brooklyn force with that of New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me,_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me%2C_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg/175px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me%2C_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg" width="175" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me%2C_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg/263px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me%2C_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me%2C_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg/350px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me%2C_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_%22Any_Thing_for_Me,_If_You_Please%3F%22--Post_Office_of_the_Brooklyn_Fair_in_Aid_of_the_Sanitary_Commission_-_Winslow_Homer_-_overall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Any Thing for Me, if You Please?" Post Office, 1864</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fervent in the Union cause, the city of Brooklyn played a major role in supplying troops and <a href="/wiki/Materiel" title="Materiel">materiel</a> for the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. The most well-known regiment to be sent off to war from the city was the <a href="/wiki/14th_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="14th Brooklyn">14th Brooklyn</a> <i>"Red Legged Devils"</i>. They fought from 1861 to 1864, wore red the entire war, and were the only regiment named after a city; President Lincoln called them into service personally, making them part of a handful of three-year enlisted soldiers in April 1861. Unlike other regiments during the American Civil War, the 14th wore a uniform inspired by that of the French <a href="/wiki/Chasseur" title="Chasseur">Chasseurs</a>, a light infantry used for quick assaults on the enemy.</p>
<p>As both a seaport and a manufacturing center, Brooklyn was well prepared to contribute to the Union's strengths in shipping and manufacturing. The two combined in shipbuilding; the ironclad <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">Monitor</a></i> was built in Brooklyn.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_city">Twin city</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Twin city">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Brooklyn is referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Twin_cities_(geographical_proximity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin cities (geographical proximity)">twin city</a> of New York in the 1883 poem, "<a href="/wiki/The_New_Colossus" title="The New Colossus">The New Colossus</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Emma_Lazarus" title="Emma Lazarus">Emma Lazarus</a>, which appears on a plaque inside the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a>. The poem calls New York Harbor "the air-bridged harbor that twin cities frame". As a twin city to New York, it played a role in national affairs that was later overshadowed by its century-old submergence into its old partner and rival.</p>
<p>Economic growth continued, propelled by <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>, and Brooklyn established itself as the third-most populous American city for much of the 19th century. The waterfront from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gowanus_Bay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gowanus Bay (page does not exist)">Gowanus Bay</a> to <a href="/wiki/Greenpoint,_Brooklyn" title="Greenpoint, Brooklyn">Greenpoint</a> was developed with piers and factories. Industrial access to the waterfront was improved by the <a href="/wiki/Gowanus_Canal" title="Gowanus Canal">Gowanus Canal</a> and the canalized <a href="/wiki/Newtown_Creek" title="Newtown Creek">Newtown Creek</a>. The <a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">USS <i>Monitor</i></a> was only the most famous product of the large and growing <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipbuilding industry">shipbuilding industry</a> of Williamsburg. After the <a href="/wiki/US_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="US Civil War">Civil War</a>, trolley lines and other transport brought <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a> beyond <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Park_(Brooklyn)" title="Prospect Park (Brooklyn)">Prospect Park</a> and into the center of the county.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg/250px-Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg" width="250" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg/375px-Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg/500px-Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7948" data-file-height="5707" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Currier_and_Ives_Brooklyn_Bridge2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">Brooklyn Bridge</a> in 1883, by <a href="/wiki/Currier_and_Ives" title="Currier and Ives">Currier and Ives</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The rapidly growing population needed more water, so the City built centralized waterworks including the <a href="/wiki/Ridgewood_Reservoir" title="Ridgewood Reservoir">Ridgewood Reservoir</a>. The municipal Police Department, however, was abolished in 1854 in favor of a Metropolitan force covering also New York and Westchester Counties. In 1865 the Brooklyn Fire Department (BFD) also gave way to the new Metropolitan Fire District.</p>
<p>Throughout this period the peripheral towns of Kings County, far from Manhattan and even from urban Brooklyn, maintained their rustic independence. The only municipal change seen was the secession of the eastern section of the Town of Flatbush as the Town of New Lots in 1852. The building of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_City_Subway" title="History of the New York City Subway">rail links</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/BMT_Brighton_Line" title="BMT Brighton Line">Brighton Beach Line</a> in 1878 heralded the end of this isolation.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_(1900)_(14597683228).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_%281900%29_%2814597683228%29.jpg/250px-The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_%281900%29_%2814597683228%29.jpg" width="250" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_%281900%29_%2814597683228%29.jpg/375px-The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_%281900%29_%2814597683228%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_%281900%29_%2814597683228%29.jpg/500px-The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_%281900%29_%2814597683228%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2530" data-file-height="2416" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_World_almanac_and_encyclopedia_(1900)_(14597683228).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Borough of Brooklyn wards, 1900</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Brooklyn" title="Sports in Brooklyn">Sports</a> became big business, and the Brooklyn Bridegrooms played professional baseball at Washington Park in the convenient suburb of <a href="/wiki/Park_Slope,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Park Slope, Brooklyn">Park Slope</a> and elsewhere. Early in the next century, under their new name of Brooklyn Dodgers, they brought baseball to <a href="/wiki/Ebbets_Field" title="Ebbets Field">Ebbets Field</a>, beyond Prospect Park. Racetracks, <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement parks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beach_resort" class="mw-redirect" title="Beach resort">beach resorts</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Beach" title="Brighton Beach">Brighton Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island" title="Coney Island">Coney Island</a>, and elsewhere in the southern part of the county.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg/250px-Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg" width="250" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg/375px-Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg/500px-Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8635" data-file-height="5927" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Currier_%26_Ives_Brooklyn2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Currier_and_Ives" title="Currier and Ives">Currier and Ives</a> print of Brooklyn, 1886.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Toward the end of the 19th century, the City of Brooklyn experienced its final, explosive growth spurt. Railroads and industrialization spread to <a href="/wiki/Bay_Ridge,_Brooklyn" title="Bay Ridge, Brooklyn">Bay Ridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Sunset Park, Brooklyn">Sunset Park</a>. In the space of a decade, the city annexed the Town of <a href="/wiki/New_Lots,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="New Lots, Brooklyn">New Lots</a> in 1886, the Town of <a href="/wiki/Flatbush,_Brooklyn" title="Flatbush, Brooklyn">Flatbush</a>, the Town of <a href="/wiki/Gravesend,_Brooklyn" title="Gravesend, Brooklyn">Gravesend</a>, the Town of <a href="/wiki/New_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="New Utrecht">New Utrecht</a> in 1894, and the Town of <a href="/wiki/Flatlands,_Brooklyn" title="Flatlands, Brooklyn">Flatlands</a> in 1896. Brooklyn had reached its natural municipal boundaries at the ends of Kings County.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayors_of_the_City_of_Brooklyn">Mayors of the City of Brooklyn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mayors of the City of Brooklyn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_New_York_City" title="List of mayors of New York City">List of mayors of New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borough_President#Brooklyn_Borough_Presidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Borough President">Brooklyn borough presidents</a></div>
<p>Brooklyn elected a mayor from 1834 until consolidation in 1898 into the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Greater_New_York" title="City of Greater New York">City of Greater New York</a>, whose own second mayor (1902–1903), <a href="/wiki/Seth_Low" title="Seth Low">Seth Low</a>, had been Mayor of Brooklyn from 1882 to 1885. Since 1898, Brooklyn has, in place of a separate mayor, elected a <a href="/wiki/Borough_President" class="mw-redirect" title="Borough President">Borough President</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_City_borough">New York City borough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: New York City borough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_City_(1898%E2%80%931945)" title="History of New York City (1898–1945)">History of New York City (1898–1945)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg/250px-1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg" width="250" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg/375px-1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg/500px-1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4134" data-file-height="3084" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1897_Brooklyn_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brooklyn in 1897</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1883, the Brooklyn Bridge was completed, transportation to Manhattan was no longer by water only, and the City of Brooklyn's ties to the City of New York were strengthened.</p>
<p>The question became whether Brooklyn was prepared to engage in the still-grander process of consolidation then developing throughout the region, whether to join with the county of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">New York</a>, the county of <a href="/wiki/Richmond_County,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Richmond County, New York">Richmond</a> and the western portion of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens County</a> to form the five boroughs of a united City of New York. <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Haskell_Green" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew Haskell Green">Andrew Haskell Green</a> and other progressives said Yes, and eventually they prevailed against the <i><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Eagle" title="Brooklyn Eagle">Daily Eagle</a></i> and other conservative forces. In 1894, residents of Brooklyn and the other counties voted by a slight majority to merge, effective in 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kings County retained its status as one of New York State's counties, but the loss of Brooklyn's separate identity as a city was met with consternation by some residents at the time. The merger was called the "Great Mistake of 1898" by many newspapers of the day, and the phrase still denotes Brooklyn pride among old-time Brooklynites.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Brooklyn totals 97 square miles (250&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) in area, of which 71 square miles (180&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) is land (73%), and 26 square miles (67&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) is water (27%); the borough is the second-largest in land area among the boroughs of New York City. However, Kings County, coterminous with Brooklyn, is New York State's fourth-smallest <a href="/wiki/County_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="County (New York)">county</a> by land area and third-smallest by total area.<sup id="cite_ref-GR1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-4">[4]</a></sup> Brooklyn lies at the southwestern end of Long Island, and the borough's western border constitutes the island's western tip. Brooklyn's water borders are extensive and varied, including <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Bay" title="Jamaica Bay">Jamaica Bay</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>; <a href="/wiki/The_Narrows" title="The Narrows">The Narrows</a>, separating Brooklyn from the borough of <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a> in New York City and crossed by the <a href="/wiki/Verrazano%E2%80%93Narrows_Bridge" title="Verrazano–Narrows Bridge">Verrazano–Narrows Bridge</a>; <a href="/wiki/Upper_New_York_Bay" title="Upper New York Bay">Upper New York Bay</a>, separating Brooklyn from <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">Jersey City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayonne,_New_Jersey" title="Bayonne, New Jersey">Bayonne</a> in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">East River</a>, separating Brooklyn from the borough of Manhattan in New York City and traversed by the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn-Battery_Tunnel" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn-Battery Tunnel">Brooklyn-Battery Tunnel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">Brooklyn Bridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Bridge" title="Manhattan Bridge">Manhattan Bridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg_Bridge" title="Williamsburg Bridge">Williamsburg Bridge</a>, and numerous routes of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a>. To the east of Brooklyn lies the borough of Queens, which contains <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> in that borough's <a href="/wiki/Howard_Beach,_Queens" title="Howard Beach, Queens">Howard Beach</a> neighborhood, approximately two miles from the border of the <a href="/wiki/East_New_York,_Brooklyn" title="East New York, Brooklyn">East New York</a> neighborhood of Brooklyn.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughscape">Boroughscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Boroughscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1808px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;direction:rtl;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Skyline_(9910358874).jpg" class="image" title="The Downtown Brooklyn skyline, the Manhattan Bridge (far left), and the Brooklyn Bridge (near left) are seen across the East River from Lower Manhattan at sunset in 2013."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Brooklyn_Skyline_%289910358874%29.jpg/1800px-Brooklyn_Skyline_%289910358874%29.jpg" width="1800" height="363" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Brooklyn_Skyline_%289910358874%29.jpg/2700px-Brooklyn_Skyline_%289910358874%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Brooklyn_Skyline_%289910358874%29.jpg/3600px-Brooklyn_Skyline_%289910358874%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8894" data-file-height="1793" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Skyline_(9910358874).jpg" title="File:Brooklyn Skyline (9910358874).jpg"></a></div>
<div align="center">The <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Brooklyn" title="Downtown Brooklyn">Downtown Brooklyn</a> <a href="/wiki/Skyline" title="Skyline">skyline</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Bridge" title="Manhattan Bridge">Manhattan Bridge</a> (far left), and the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">Brooklyn Bridge</a> (near left) are seen across the <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">East River</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a> at sunset in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, using the 32&#160;°F (0&#160;°C) coldest month (January) <a href="/wiki/Isotherm_(contour_line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Isotherm (contour line)">isotherm</a>, Brooklyn experiences a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<i>Cfa</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-Peel.2C_M._C..3B_Finlayson.2C_B._L..3B_McMahon.2C_T._A_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peel.2C_M._C..3B_Finlayson.2C_B._L..3B_McMahon.2C_T._A-23">[23]</a></sup> with partial shielding from the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> and moderating influences from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. Brooklyn receives plentiful precipitation all year round, with nearly 50&#160;in (1,300&#160;mm) yearly. The area averages 234 days with at least some sunshine annually, and averages 57% of possible sunshine annually, accumulating 2,535 hours of sunshine per annum.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Brooklyn lies in the <a href="/wiki/USDA" class="mw-redirect" title="USDA">USDA</a> <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">7b plant hardiness zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">

<p>Since 2010, the population of Brooklyn was estimated by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> to have increased 5.3% to 2,636,735, as of 2015 – Brooklyn's estimated population represented 30.8% of New York City's estimated population of 8,550,405; 33.6% of Long Island's population of 7,838,722; and 13.3% of New York State's population of 19,795,791.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCest_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCest-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kings_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kings_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QueensQuickFacts_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QueensQuickFacts-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nassau_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nassau_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U.S._Census_Bureau_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Census_Bureau-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYSQuickFacts_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYSQuickFacts-41">[41]</a></sup></p>

<a href="/wiki/Haredi_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Haredi Jews">Ultra-Orthodox</a> <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_New_York_City" title="Jews in New York City">Jewish (יהודי)</a> residents in Brooklyn, home to the largest Jewish community in the United States, with approximately 600,000 individuals, about 23% <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> of the borough's population in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></div>

</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_Census">2010 Census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2010 Census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, Brooklyn's population was 42.8% <a href="/wiki/White_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White American">White</a>, including 35.7% <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_White" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Hispanic White">non-Hispanic White</a>; 34.3% <a href="/wiki/Black_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Black American">Black</a>, including 31.9% non-Hispanic black; 10.5% <a href="/wiki/Asian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian American">Asian</a>; 0.5% <a href="/wiki/Native_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Native American">Native American</a>; 0.0% (rounded) <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander American">Pacific Islander</a>; 3.0% <a href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiracial American">Multiracial American</a>; and 8.8% from <a href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (United States Census)">Other races</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic and Latino American">Hispanics and Latinos</a> made up 19.8% of Brooklyn's population.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a6/Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park%2C_Brooklyn.jpg/250px-Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park%2C_Brooklyn.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a6/Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park%2C_Brooklyn.jpg/375px-Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park%2C_Brooklyn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a6/Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park%2C_Brooklyn.jpg/500px-Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park%2C_Brooklyn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Celebrating_Chinese_New_Year_on_8th_Avenue_Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Celebrating <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Fuzhou#Little_Fuzhou.2C_Brooklyn" title="Little Fuzhou">Little Fuzhou (小福州)</a></i>, one of several <a href="/wiki/Chinatowns_in_Brooklyn#Chinatownscape" title="Chinatowns in Brooklyn">Chinatowns in Brooklyn (布鲁克林華埠)</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Sunset Park, Brooklyn">Sunset Park (日落公園)</a>. Brooklyn's rapidly growing <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans_in_New_York_City" title="Chinese Americans in New York City">Chinese American</a> population was estimated to have surpassed 200,000 in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_estimates">2012 estimates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2012 estimates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the 2012 U.S. Census Bureau estimates, there are 2,565,635 people (up from 2.3&#160;million in 1990), 880,727 households, and 583,922 families living in Brooklyn.<sup id="cite_ref-GR2_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The population density was 34,920/square&#160;mile (13,480/km²). There were 930,866 housing units at an average density of 13,180/square&#160;mile (5,090/km²).</p>
<p>Of the 880,727 households in Brooklyn, 38.6% were married couples living together, 22.3% had a female householder with no husband present, and 33.7% were non-families. 33.3% had children under the age of 18 living in them. Of all households 27.8% are made up of individuals and 9.8% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.75 and the average family size was 3.41.</p>
<p>In Brooklyn the population was spread out with 26.9% under the age of 18, 10.3% from 18 to 24, 30.8% from 25 to 44, 20.6% from 45 to 64, and 11.5% who are 65 years of age or older. The median age was 33 years. Brooklyn has more women and girls, with 88.4 males for every 100 females. Brooklyn's <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbian</a> community is the largest out of all of the New York City boroughs.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The median income for households in Brooklyn was $32,135, and the median income for a family was $36,188. Males had a median income of $34,317, which was higher than females, whose median income was $30,516. The per capita income was $16,775. About 22% of families and 25.1% of the population were below the poverty line, including 34% of those under age 18 and 21.5% of those age 65 or over.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Brooklyn has a high degree of <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_diversity_index" title="Linguistic diversity index">linguistic diversity</a>. As of 2010, 54.12% (1,240,416) of Brooklyn residents ages 5 and older spoke <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> at home as a <a href="/wiki/Primary_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary language">primary language</a>, while 17.16% (393,340) spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, 6.46% (148,012) <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, 5.31% (121,607) <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, 3.47% (79,469) <a href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Yiddish language">Yiddish</a>, 2.75% (63,019) <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French Creole</a>, 1.35% (31,004) <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, 1.20% (27,440) <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>, 1.01% (23,207) <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, 0.99% (22,763) <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, 0.95% (21,773) <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, 0.85% (19,388) <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">various Indic languages</a>, 0.70% (15,936) <a href="/wiki/Urdu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African languages</a> were spoken as a <a href="/wiki/Main_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Main language">main language</a> by 0.54% (12,305) of the population over the age of five. In total, 45.88% (1,051,456) of Brooklyn's population ages 5 and older spoke a <a href="/wiki/Mother_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother language">mother language</a> other than English.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">Neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brooklyn_neighborhoods" title="List of Brooklyn neighborhoods">List of Brooklyn neighborhoods</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_ethnic_enclaves" title="New York City ethnic enclaves">New York City ethnic enclaves</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greenpoint_Houses.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Greenpoint_Houses.JPG/250px-Greenpoint_Houses.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Greenpoint_Houses.JPG/375px-Greenpoint_Houses.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Greenpoint_Houses.JPG/500px-Greenpoint_Houses.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
