Middagh Street, Brooklyn Heights</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brooklyn's neighborhoods are dynamic in ethnic composition. For example, during the early to mid-20th century, <a href="/wiki/Brownsville,_Brooklyn" title="Brownsville, Brooklyn">Brownsville</a> had a majority of <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_New_York_City" title="Jews in New York City">Jewish</a> residents; since the 1970s it has been majority African American. <a href="/wiki/Midwood,_Brooklyn" title="Midwood, Brooklyn">Midwood</a> during the early 20th century was filled with ethnic <a href="/wiki/Irish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish American">Irish</a>, then filled with Jewish residents for nearly 50 years, and is slowly becoming a <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistani American">Pakistani</a> enclave. Brooklyn's most populous racial group, white, declined from 97.2% in 1930 to 46.9% by 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-Gibson2005_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson2005-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Along with <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a>, many of Brooklyn's neighborhoods are also becoming increasingly diverse, with an influx of immigrants integrating its neighborhoods. The borough also attracts people previously living in other cities in the United States. Of these, most come from <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US_Census_Bureau.2C_California.2C_racial_breakdown_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_Census_Bureau.2C_California.2C_racial_breakdown-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_diversity">Community diversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Community diversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Given New York City's role as a crossroads for legal and illegal immigration from around the world, Brooklyn has evolved a globally <a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitanism" title="Cosmopolitanism">cosmopolitan</a> ambience of its own, demonstrating a robust and growing demographic and cultural diversity with respect to metrics including nationality, religion, race, and <a href="/wiki/Domestic_partnership" title="Domestic partnership">domiciliary partnership</a>. Brooklyn contains dozens of distinct neighborhoods representing many of the major culturally identified groups found within New York City. Among the most prominent are listed below:</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jewish_American">Jewish American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Jewish American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_New_York_City" title="Jews in New York City">Jews in New York City</a></div>
<p>Over 600,000 <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Jews">Orthodox Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hasidic_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Hasidic Jews">Hasidic Jews</a>, have become concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Borough_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Borough Park, Brooklyn">Borough Park</a>, Williamsburg, and <a href="/wiki/Flatbush,_Brooklyn" title="Flatbush, Brooklyn">Flatbush</a>, where there are many <a href="/wiki/Yeshiva" title="Yeshiva">yeshivas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kosher" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosher">kosher</a> <a href="/wiki/Delicatessen" title="Delicatessen">delicatessens</a>, as well as many other Jewish businesses. Other notable religious Orthodox and <a href="/wiki/Hasidic_Judaism" title="Hasidic Judaism">Hasidic Jewish</a> neighborhoods are <a href="/wiki/Kensington,_Brooklyn" title="Kensington, Brooklyn">Kensington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midwood,_Brooklyn" title="Midwood, Brooklyn">Midwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canarsie,_Brooklyn" title="Canarsie, Brooklyn">Canarsie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_Gate,_Brooklyn" title="Sea Gate, Brooklyn">Sea Gate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Crown_Heights,_Brooklyn" title="Crown Heights, Brooklyn">Crown Heights</a>. Many hospitals in Brooklyn were started by Jewish charities, including <a href="/wiki/Maimonides_Medical_Center" title="Maimonides Medical Center">Maimonides Medical Center</a> in Borough Park and Brookdale Hospital in Brownsville.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Many non-religious Jews are concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Ditmas_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Ditmas Park, Brooklyn">Ditmas Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Terrace,_Brooklyn" title="Windsor Terrace, Brooklyn">Windsor Terrace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Park_Slope,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Park Slope, Brooklyn">Park Slope</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_American">Chinese American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Chinese American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Chinatowns_in_Brooklyn" title="Chinatowns in Brooklyn">Chinatowns in Brooklyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans_in_New_York_City" title="Chinese Americans in New York City">Chinese Americans in New York City</a></div>
<p>Over 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans_in_New_York_City" title="Chinese Americans in New York City">Chinese Americans</a> live throughout the southern parts of Brooklyn, in <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Sunset Park, Brooklyn">Sunset Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bensonhurst,_Brooklyn" title="Bensonhurst, Brooklyn">Bensonhurst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gravesend,_Brooklyn" title="Gravesend, Brooklyn">Gravesend</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Homecrest,_Brooklyn" title="Homecrest, Brooklyn">Homecrest</a>. The largest concentration is in <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Sunset Park, Brooklyn">Sunset Park</a> along 8th Avenue, which is known for <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Culture of China">Chinese</a> culture. It is called <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinatown, Brooklyn">"Brooklyn's Chinatown"</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> population is composed in majority by <a href="/wiki/Fuzhounese_Americans" title="Fuzhounese Americans">Fuzhounese Americans</a>, rendering this Chinatown with the nicknames <i><a href="/wiki/Chinatowns_in_Brooklyn#Fuzhou_Town_.28.E7.A6.8F.E5.B7.9E.E5.9F.A0.29.2C_Brooklyn_.28.E5.B8.83.E9.B2.81.E5.85.8B.E6.9E.97.29" title="Chinatowns in Brooklyn">Fuzhou Town (福州埠), Brooklyn (布鲁克林)</a></i> or the <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Fuzhou" title="Little Fuzhou">Little Fuzhou (小福州)</a></i> of Brooklyn. Many <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese restaurants</a> can be found throughout Sunset Park, and the area hosts a popular <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> celebration.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean_and_African_American">Caribbean and African American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Caribbean and African American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Caribbeans_in_New_York_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbeans in New York City">Caribbeans in New York City</a></div>
<p>Brooklyn's African American and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> communities are spread throughout much of Brooklyn. Brooklyn's <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> community is concentrated in the Crown Heights, Flatbush, <a href="/wiki/East_Flatbush,_Brooklyn" title="East Flatbush, Brooklyn">East Flatbush</a>, Kensington, and Canarsie neighborhoods in central Brooklyn. Brooklyn is home to one of the largest communities of West Indians outside of the Caribbean, being rivaled only by Toronto, Miami, Montreal, and London. Although the largest West Indian groups in Brooklyn are mostly <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamaican American">Jamaicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyanese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Guyanese American">Guyanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Americans" title="Haitian Americans">Haitians</a>, there are <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indian American">West Indian immigrants</a> from nearly every part of the Caribbean. Crown Heights and Flatbush are home to many of Brooklyn's West Indian restaurants and bakeries. Brooklyn has an annual, celebrated Carnival in the tradition of pre-Lenten celebrations in the islands. Started by natives of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day_Carnival" title="Labor Day Carnival">West Indian Labor Day Parade</a> takes place every Labor Day on <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Parkway_(Brooklyn)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Parkway (Brooklyn)">Eastern Parkway</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bedford-Stuyvesant,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Bedford-Stuyvesant, Brooklyn">Bedford-Stuyvesant</a> is home to one of the most famous African American communities in the city, along with <a href="/wiki/Brownsville,_Brooklyn" title="Brownsville, Brooklyn">Brownsville</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="East New York">East New York</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Coney Island, Brooklyn">Coney Island</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Latino_American">Latino American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Latino American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_migration_to_New_York_City" title="Puerto Rican migration to New York City">Puerto Rican migration to New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuyorican" title="Nuyorican">Nuyorican</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bushwick,_Brooklyn" title="Bushwick, Brooklyn">Bushwick</a> is the largest hub of Brooklyn's <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic American</a> community. Like other Hispanic neighborhoods in New York City, Bushwick has an established <a href="/wiki/Stateside_Puerto_Ricans" class="mw-redirect" title="Stateside Puerto Ricans">Puerto Rican</a> presence, along with an influx of many <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Americans_(Dominican_Republic)" title="Dominican Americans (Dominican Republic)">Dominicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_American" class="mw-redirect" title="South American">South Americans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Central American">Central Americans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican people">Mexicans</a>, as well as a more recent influx of Puerto Ricans. As nearly 80% of Bushwick's population is Hispanic, its residents having created many businesses to support their various national and distinct traditions in food and other items. <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Sunset Park, Brooklyn">Sunset Park</a>'s population is 42% Hispanic, made up of these various ethnic groups. Brooklyn's main Hispanic groups are Puerto Ricans, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican American">Mexicans</a>, Dominicans, and <a href="/wiki/Panamanian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Panamanian American">Panamanians</a>; they are spread out throughout the borough. Puerto Ricans and Dominicans are predominant in Bushwick, <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Brooklyn" title="Williamsburg, Brooklyn">Williamsburg</a>, and East New York, while Mexicans are predominant in Sunset Park and Panamanians in <a href="/wiki/Crown_Heights,_Brooklyn" title="Crown Heights, Brooklyn">Crown Heights</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_and_Ukrainian_American">Russian and Ukrainian American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Russian and Ukrainian American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Americans_in_New_York_City" title="Russian Americans in New York City">Russian Americans in New York City</a></div>
<p>Brooklyn is also home to many <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, who are mainly concentrated in the areas of <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Beach,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Brighton Beach, Brooklyn">Brighton Beach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheepshead_Bay,_Brooklyn" title="Sheepshead Bay, Brooklyn">Sheepshead Bay</a>. Brighton Beach features many Russian and Ukrainian businesses and has been nicknamed <i><a href="/wiki/Russian_Americans_in_New_York_City#Russiantownscape" title="Russian Americans in New York City">Little Russia</a></i> and <i>Little <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a></i>, respectively. Originally these communities were mostly Jewish; however, the non-Jewish Russian and Ukrainian communities of Brighton Beach now also represent various aspects of Russian and Ukrainian culture.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish_American">Polish American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Polish American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Brooklyn's <a href="/wiki/Polish-Americans" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish-Americans">Polish</a> are largely concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Greenpoint,_Brooklyn" title="Greenpoint, Brooklyn">Greenpoint</a>, which is home to <a href="/wiki/Little_Poland,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Little Poland, Brooklyn">Little Poland</a>. They are also scattered throughout the southern parts of Brooklyn.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_American">Italian American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Italian American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Italians_in_New_York_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Italians in New York City">Italians in New York City</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Italian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian American">Italian Americans</a> are mainly concentrated in the neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Bensonhurst" class="mw-redirect" title="Bensonhurst">Bensonhurst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dyker_Heights,_Brooklyn" title="Dyker Heights, Brooklyn">Dyker Heights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Ridge,_Brooklyn" title="Bay Ridge, Brooklyn">Bay Ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath_Beach,_Brooklyn" title="Bath Beach, Brooklyn">Bath Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobble_Hill,_Brooklyn" title="Cobble Hill, Brooklyn">Cobble Hill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carroll_Gardens,_Brooklyn" title="Carroll Gardens, Brooklyn">Carroll Gardens</a> where there are many Italian restaurants, bakeries, delicatessens, pizzerias, cafes, and social clubs.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim_American">Muslim American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Muslim American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Today, <a href="/wiki/Arab_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab American">Arab Americans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistani American">Pakistani Americans</a> along with other Muslim communities have moved into the southwest portion of Brooklyn, particularly to <a href="/wiki/Bay_Ridge,_Brooklyn" title="Bay Ridge, Brooklyn">Bay Ridge</a>, where there are many Middle Eastern restaurants, hookah lounges, halal shops, Islamic shops and mosques. Coney Island Avenue is home to <i>Little <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a></i> as Church Avenue is to Bangladeshis. Jay Street Borough Hall (Downtown Brooklyn) is little Arabia. Pakistani Independence Day is celebrated every year with parades and parties on Coney Island Avenue. Earlier, the area was known predominately for its Irish, Norwegian, and Scottish populations. There are also many Middle Eastern, particularly Yemeni, businesses, mosques, and restaurants on <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Avenue_(New_York_City)" title="Atlantic Avenue (New York City)">Atlantic Avenue</a> west of <a href="/wiki/Flatbush_Avenue" title="Flatbush Avenue">Flatbush Avenue</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Heights" title="Brooklyn Heights">Brooklyn Heights</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_American">Irish American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Irish American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Irish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish American">Irish Americans</a> can be found throughout Brooklyn, in low to moderate concentrations in the neighborhoods of Bay Ridge, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Park,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Park, Brooklyn">Marine Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerritsen_Beach,_Brooklyn" title="Gerritsen Beach, Brooklyn">Gerritsen Beach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vinegar_Hill,_Brooklyn" title="Vinegar Hill, Brooklyn">Vinegar Hill</a>. Many moved east on Long Island in the mid-twentieth century.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_American">Greek American</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Greek American">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Brooklyn's <a href="/wiki/Greek_Americans" title="Greek Americans">Greek Americans</a> live throughout the borough, but their businesses today are concentrated in Downtown Brooklyn near Atlantic Avenue. Greek-owned diners are also found throughout the borough, but many Greeks have re-located off of Atlantic Avenue due to demographic shift.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Same-sex_couples">Same-sex couples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Same-sex couples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_New_York" title="Same-sex marriage in New York">Same-sex marriage in New York</a></div>
<p>Brooklyn is home to a large and growing of same-sex couples. <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_New_York" title="Same-sex marriage in New York">Same-sex marriages in New York</a> were legalized on June 24, 2011 and were authorized to take place beginning 30 days thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Park_Slope,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="Park Slope, Brooklyn">Park Slope</a> neighborhood spearheaded the popularity of Brooklyn among <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbians</a>, and numerous neighborhoods have since become home to <a href="/wiki/LGBTQ" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBTQ">LGBTQ</a> communities.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Artists-in-residence">Artists-in-residence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Artists-in-residence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Brooklyn became a preferred site for artists and <a href="/wiki/Hipster_(contemporary_subculture)" title="Hipster (contemporary subculture)">hipsters</a> to set up live/work spaces after being priced out of the same types of living arrangements in Manhattan. Various neighborhoods in Brooklyn, including Williamsburg, <a href="/wiki/Dumbo,_Brooklyn" title="Dumbo, Brooklyn">DUMBO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Hook,_Brooklyn" title="Red Hook, Brooklyn">Red Hook</a>, and Park Slope evolved as popular neighborhoods for <a href="/wiki/Artists-in-residence" class="mw-redirect" title="Artists-in-residence">artists-in-residence</a>. However, rents and costs of living have since increased dramatically in these same neighborhoods, forcing artists to move to somewhat less expensive neighborhoods in Brooklyn or across Upper New York Bay to locales in New Jersey, such as <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">Jersey City</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hoboken,_New_Jersey" title="Hoboken, New Jersey">Hoboken</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_and_politics_in_Brooklyn" title="Government and politics in Brooklyn">Government and politics in Brooklyn</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG/250px-Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG" width="250" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG/375px-Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG/500px-Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3732" data-file-height="2626" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bk_Boro_Hall_summer_dusk_jeh.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Borough_Hall" title="Brooklyn Borough Hall">Brooklyn Borough Hall</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since consolidation with New York City in 1898, Brooklyn has been governed by the New York City Charter that provides for a "strong" <a href="/wiki/Mayor-council_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor-council government">mayor-council system</a>. The centralized <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_York_City" title="Government of New York City">government of New York City</a> is responsible for <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Education" title="New York City Department of Education">public education</a>, correctional institutions, public safety, recreational facilities, sanitation, water supply, and welfare services. On the other hand, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Public_Library" title="Brooklyn Public Library">Brooklyn Public Library</a> is an independent <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">nonprofit organization</a> partially funded by the government of New York City, but also by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_York_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of New York State">government of New York State</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the United States">U.S. federal government</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fundraising" title="Fundraising">private donors</a>.</p>
<p>The office of <a href="/wiki/Borough_President" class="mw-redirect" title="Borough President">Borough President</a> was created in the consolidation of 1898 to balance centralization with local authority. Each borough president had a powerful administrative role derived from having a vote on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Board_of_Estimate" title="New York City Board of Estimate">New York City Board of Estimate</a>, which was responsible for creating and approving the city's budget and proposals for land use. In 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> declared the Board of Estimate unconstitutional because Brooklyn, the most populous borough, had no greater effective representation on the Board than Staten Island, the least populous borough; it was a violation of the high court's <a href="/wiki/Reynolds_v._Sims" title="Reynolds v. Sims">1964 "one man, one vote" reading</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Fourteenth Amendment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 1990 the Borough President has acted as an advocate for the borough at the mayoral agencies, the City Council, the New York state government, and corporations. Brooklyn's current Borough President is <a href="/wiki/Eric_Adams_(politician)" title="Eric Adams (politician)">Eric Adams</a>, elected as a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> in November 2013 with 90.8% of the vote. Adams replaced popular Borough President <a href="/wiki/Marty_Markowitz" title="Marty Markowitz">Marty Markowitz</a>, also a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a>, who partially used his office to promote tourism and new development for Brooklyn.</p>
<p>The Democratic Party holds the majority of public offices. As of 2005, 69.7% of registered voters in Brooklyn were Democrats. Party platforms center on affordable housing, education and economic development. The most controversial political issue is the proposed <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Yards" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Yards">Atlantic Yards</a>, a large housing and sports arena project. Pockets of majority Republican influence exist in Gravesend, Bensonhurst, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Ridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay Ridge">Bay Ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dyker_Heights" class="mw-redirect" title="Dyker Heights">Dyker Heights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midwood" class="mw-redirect" title="Midwood">Midwood</a> by U.S. Representative Dan Donovan and New York State Senator Marty Golden.</p>
<p>Each of the city's five counties (coterminous with each borough) has its own criminal court system and <a href="/wiki/District_Attorney" class="mw-redirect" title="District Attorney">District Attorney</a>, the chief public prosecutor who is directly elected by popular vote. The District Attorney of Kings County is Eric Gonzalez, who replaced Democrat <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_P._Thompson" title="Kenneth P. Thompson">Kenneth P. Thompson</a> following his death in October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Brooklyn has 16 City Council members, the largest number of any of the five boroughs. Brooklyn has 18 of the city's 59 community districts, each served by an unpaid Community Board with advisory powers under the city's Uniform Land Use Review Procedure. Each board has a paid district manager who acts as an interlocutor with city agencies.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_New_York_City" title="Economy of New York City">Economy of New York City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_(BB-55),_June_1940.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_%28BB-55%29%2C_June_1940.jpg/250px-Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_%28BB-55%29%2C_June_1940.jpg" width="250" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_%28BB-55%29%2C_June_1940.jpg/375px-Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_%28BB-55%29%2C_June_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_%28BB-55%29%2C_June_1940.jpg/500px-Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_%28BB-55%29%2C_June_1940.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="550" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Launching_of_USS_North_Carolina_(BB-55),_June_1940.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/USS_North_Carolina_(BB-55)" title="USS North Carolina (BB-55)">USS <i>North Carolina</i></a>, launched at <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Navy_Yard" title="Brooklyn Navy Yard">Brooklyn Navy Yard</a>, June 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG/250px-Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG/375px-Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG/500px-Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_buildings_near_East_River_IMG_3731.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Newer buildings near <a href="/wiki/East_River_State_Park" title="East River State Park">East River State Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brooklyn's job market is driven by three main factors: the performance of the national and city economy, population flows and the borough's position as a convenient back office for New York's businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-report_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Forty-four percent of Brooklyn's employed population, or 410,000 people, work in the borough; more than half of the borough's residents work outside its boundaries. As a result, economic conditions in Manhattan are important to the borough's jobseekers. Strong international immigration to Brooklyn generates jobs in services, retailing and construction.<sup id="cite_ref-report_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the late 20th century, Brooklyn has benefited from a steady influx of financial <a href="/wiki/Back_office" title="Back office">back office</a> operations from Manhattan, the rapid growth of a <a href="/wiki/High-tech" class="mw-redirect" title="High-tech">high-tech</a> and entertainment economy in <a href="/wiki/DUMBO,_Brooklyn" class="mw-redirect" title="DUMBO, Brooklyn">DUMBO</a>, and strong growth in support services such as accounting, personal supply agencies, and computer services firms.<sup id="cite_ref-report_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jobs in the borough have traditionally been concentrated in manufacturing, but since 1975, Brooklyn has shifted from a manufacturing-based to a service-based economy. In 2004, 215,000 Brooklyn residents worked in the services sector, while 27,500 worked in manufacturing. Although manufacturing has declined, a substantial base has remained in apparel and niche manufacturing concerns such as furniture, fabricated metals, and food products.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The pharmaceutical company <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a> was founded in Brooklyn in 1869 and had a manufacturing plant in the borough for many years that once employed thousands of workers, but the plant shut down in 2008. However, new light-manufacturing concerns packaging organic and high-end food have sprung up in the old plant.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>First established as a <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a> facility in 1801, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Navy_Yard" title="Brooklyn Navy Yard">Brooklyn Navy Yard</a> employed 70,000 people at its peak during World War II and was then the largest employer in the borough. The <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Missouri_(BB-63)" title="USS Missouri (BB-63)">Missouri</a></i>, the ship on which the Japanese formally surrendered, was built there, as was the <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Maine_(ACR-1)" title="USS Maine (ACR-1)">Maine</a></i>, whose sinking off Havana led to the start of the Spanish–American War. The iron-sided Civil War vessel the <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">Monitor</a></i> was built in Greenpoint. From 1968–1979 <a href="/wiki/Seatrain_Lines" title="Seatrain Lines">Seatrain Shipbuilding</a> was the major employer.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Later tenants include industrial design firms, food processing businesses, artisans, and the film and television production industry. About 230 private-sector firms providing 4,000 jobs are at the Yard.</p>
<p>Construction and services are the fastest growing sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Most employers in Brooklyn are small businesses. In 2000, 91% of the approximately 38,704 business establishments in Brooklyn had fewer than 20 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> As of August 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the borough's unemployment rate was 5.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brooklyn is also home to many banks and <a href="/wiki/Credit_union" title="Credit union">credit unions</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation</a>, there were 37 banks and 26 credit unions operating in the borough in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Zoning_in_the_United_States" title="Zoning in the United States">rezoning</a> of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Brooklyn" title="Downtown Brooklyn">Downtown Brooklyn</a> has generated over US$10 billion of private investment and $300 million in public improvements since 2004. Brooklyn is also attracting numerous <a href="/wiki/High_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="High technology">high technology</a> <a href="/wiki/Start-up_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Start-up company">start-up companies</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Alley" title="Silicon Alley">Silicon Alley</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Metonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Metonym">metonym</a> for New York City's <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship_ecosystem" title="Entrepreneurship ecosystem">entrepreneurship ecosystem</a>, has expanded from <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a> into Brooklyn.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_York_City" title="Culture of New York City">Culture of New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_of_New_York_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of New York City">Media of New York City</a></div>

<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brooklyn" title="Culture of Brooklyn">Culture of Brooklyn</a></div>
<p>Brooklyn has played a major role in various aspects of American culture including literature, cinema, and theater. The <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_accent" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn accent">Brooklyn accent</a> has often been portrayed as the "typical New York accent" in American media, although this accent and stereotype are supposedly fading out.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Brooklyn's official colors are blue and gold.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_venues">Cultural venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cultural venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Brooklyn hosts the world-renowned <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Academy_of_Music" title="Brooklyn Academy of Music">Brooklyn Academy of Music</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Philharmonic" title="Brooklyn Philharmonic">Brooklyn Philharmonic</a>, and the second largest public art collection in the United States, housed in the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a>, opened in 1897, is New York City's second-largest public art museum. It has in its permanent collection more than 1.5&#160;million objects, from ancient Egyptian masterpieces to contemporary art. The <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Children%27s_Museum" title="Brooklyn Children's Museum">Brooklyn Children's Museum</a>, the world's first museum dedicated to children, opened in December 1899. The only such New York State institution accredited by the <a href="/wiki/American_Alliance_of_Museums" title="American Alliance of Museums">American Alliance of Museums</a>, it is one of the few globally to have a permanent collection&#160;– over 30,000 cultural objects and natural history specimens.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Academy_of_Music" title="Brooklyn Academy of Music">Brooklyn Academy of Music</a> (BAM) includes a 2,109-seat opera house, an 874-seat theater, and the art house BAM Rose Cinemas. <a href="/wiki/Bargemusic" title="Bargemusic">Bargemusic</a> and St. Ann's Warehouse are located on the other side of Downtown Brooklyn in the <a href="/wiki/DUMBO" class="mw-redirect" title="DUMBO">DUMBO</a> arts district. <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Technical_High_School" title="Brooklyn Technical High School">Brooklyn Technical High School</a> has the second-largest auditorium in New York City (after <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a>), with a seating capacity of over 3,000.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_periodicals">Local periodicals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Local periodicals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Brooklyn has several local newspapers: The <i><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Eagle" title="Brooklyn Eagle">Brooklyn Daily Eagle</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bay_Currents" title="Bay Currents">Bay Currents</a></i> (Oceanfront Brooklyn), <i>Brooklyn View</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Brooklyn_Paper" title="The Brooklyn Paper">The Brooklyn Paper</a></i>, and Courier-Life Publications. Courier-Life Publications, owned by Rupert Murdoch's <a href="/wiki/News_Corporation" title="News Corporation">News Corporation</a>, is Brooklyn's largest chain of newspapers. Brooklyn is also served by the major New York dailies, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">New York Daily News</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i>.</p>
<p>The borough is home to the bi-weekly cultural guide <i><a href="/wiki/The_L_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="The L Magazine">The L Magazine</a></i> and the arts and politics monthly <i><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Rail">Brooklyn Rail</a></i>, as well as the arts and cultural quarterly <i><a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(magazine)" title="Cabinet (magazine)">Cabinet</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Hello_Mr." title="Hello Mr.">Hello Mr.</a></i> is also published in Brooklyn.</p>
<p><i>Brooklyn Magazine</i> is one of the few glossy magazines about Brooklyn. Several others, that are now defunct, include: <i>BKLYN Magazine</i> (a bimonthly lifestyle book owned by Joseph McCarthy, that saw itself as a vehicle for high-end advertisers in Manhattan and was mailed to 80,000 high-income households), <i>Brooklyn Bridge Magazine</i>, <i>The Brooklynite</i> (a free, glossy quarterly edited by Daniel Treiman), and <i>NRG</i> (edited by Gail Johnson and originally marketed as a local periodical for Clinton Hill and Fort Greene, but expanded in scope to become the self-proclaimed "Pulse of Brooklyn" and then the "Pulse of New York").<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_press">Ethnic press</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Ethnic press">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Brooklyn has a thriving ethnic press. <i><a href="/wiki/El_Diario_La_Prensa" title="El Diario La Prensa">El Diario La Prensa</a></i>, the largest and oldest Spanish-language daily newspaper in the United States, maintains its corporate headquarters at 1&#160;<a href="/wiki/MetroTech_Center" title="MetroTech Center">MetroTech Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Brooklyn" title="Downtown Brooklyn">downtown Brooklyn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Major ethnic publications include the Brooklyn-Queens Catholic paper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tablet_(Diocese_of_Brooklyn)" title="The Tablet (Diocese of Brooklyn)">The Tablet</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hamodia" title="Hamodia">Hamodia</a></i>, an Orthodox Jewish daily and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Press" title="The Jewish Press">The Jewish Press</a></i>, an Orthodox Jewish weekly. Many nationally distributed ethnic newspapers are based in Brooklyn. Over 60 ethnic groups, writing in 42 languages, publish some 300 non-English language magazines and newspapers in New York City. Among them the quarterly "<a href="/wiki/L%27Idea" title="L'Idea">L'Idea</a>", a bilingual magazine printed in Italian and English since 1974. In addition, many newspapers published abroad, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Gleaner_Company" title="Gleaner Company">The Daily Gleaner</a></i> and <i>The Star</i> of Jamaica, are available in Brooklyn.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Our_Time_Press" title="Our Time Press">Our Time Press</a> published weekly by DBG Media covers the Village of Brooklyn with a motto of "The Local paper with the Global View".</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The City of New York has an official television station, run by the <a href="/wiki/NYC_Media_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="NYC Media Group">NYC Media Group</a>, which features programming based in Brooklyn. <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Community_Access_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Community Access Television">Brooklyn Community Access Television</a> is the borough's <a href="/wiki/Public_access_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Public access television">public access channel</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The annual <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island_Mermaid_Parade" title="Coney Island Mermaid Parade">Coney Island Mermaid Parade</a> (mid-to-late June) is a costume-and-float parade.<sup id="cite_ref-Ward.2C_Nathan_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ward.2C_Nathan-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>Coney Island also hosts the annual <a href="/wiki/Nathan%27s_Hot_Dog_Eating_Contest" title="Nathan's Hot Dog Eating Contest">Nathan's Hot Dog Eating Contest</a> (July 4).<sup id="cite_ref-Ward.2C_Nathan_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ward.2C_Nathan-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>The annual <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day_Carnival" title="Labor Day Carnival">Labor Day Carnival</a> (also known as the Labor Day Parade or West Indian Day Parade) takes place along <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Parkway" title="Eastern Parkway">Eastern Parkway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Crown_Heights,_Brooklyn" title="Crown Heights, Brooklyn">Crown Heights</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_other_attractions">Parks and other attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Parks and other attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_New_York_City" title="Tourism in New York City">Tourism in New York City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ad/Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg/250px-Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ad/Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg/375px-Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ad/Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg/500px-Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="367" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bbg_cherry_esplande.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Prunus_serrulata" title="Prunus serrulata">Kwanzan Cherries</a> in bloom at <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Botanic_Garden" title="Brooklyn Botanic Garden">Brooklyn Botanic Garden</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg/250px-Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg" width="250" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg/375px-Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg/500px-Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2104" data-file-height="1180" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coney_Island_Beach-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Astroland" title="Astroland">Astroland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island" title="Coney Island">Coney Island</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Botanic_Garden" title="Brooklyn Botanic Garden">Brooklyn Botanic Garden</a>: located adjacent to Prospect Park is the 52-acre (21&#160;ha) botanical garden, which includes a cherry tree esplanade, a one-acre (0.4&#160;ha) rose garden, a Japanese hill and pond garden, a fragrance garden, a water lily pond esplanade, several conservatories, a rock garden, a native flora garden, a <i><a href="/wiki/Bonsai" title="Bonsai">bonsai</a></i> tree collection, and children's gardens and discovery exhibits.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coney_Island" title="Coney Island">Coney Island</a> developed as a playground for the rich in the early 1900s, but it grew as one of America's first amusement grounds and attracted crowds from all over New York. The <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island_Cyclone" title="Coney Island Cyclone">Cyclone rollercoaster</a>, built in 1927, is on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>. The 1920 Wonder Wheel and other rides are still operational. Coney Island went into decline in the 1970s, but has undergone a renaissance.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Floyd_Bennett_Field" title="Floyd Bennett Field">Floyd Bennett Field</a>: the first municipal airport in New York City and long closed for operations, is now part of the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_System" class="mw-redirect" title="National Park System">National Park System</a>. Many of the historic hangars and runways are still extant. Nature trails and diverse habitats are found within the park, including <a href="/wiki/Salt_marsh" title="Salt marsh">salt marsh</a> and a restored area of <a href="/wiki/Shortgrass_prairie" title="Shortgrass prairie">shortgrass prairie</a> that was once widespread on the <a href="/wiki/Hempstead_Plains" title="Hempstead Plains">Hempstead Plains</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Green-Wood_Cemetery" title="Green-Wood Cemetery">Green-Wood Cemetery</a>, founded by the social reformer Henry Evelyn Pierrepont<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> in 1838, is an early <a href="/wiki/Rural_cemetery" title="Rural cemetery">Rural cemetery</a>. It is the burial ground of many notable New Yorkers.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Bay_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Jamaica Bay Wildlife Refuge">Jamaica Bay Wildlife Refuge</a>: a unique Federal wildlife refuge straddling the Brooklyn-Queens border, part of <a href="/wiki/Gateway_National_Recreation_Area" title="Gateway National Recreation Area">Gateway National Recreation Area</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_York_Transit_Museum" title="New York Transit Museum">New York Transit Museum</a> displays historical artifacts of Greater New York's subway, commuter rail, and bus systems; it is located at Court Street, a former <a href="/wiki/Independent_Subway_System" title="Independent Subway System">Independent Subway System</a> station in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Heights" title="Brooklyn Heights">Brooklyn Heights</a> on the <a href="/wiki/IND_Fulton_Street_Line" title="IND Fulton Street Line">Fulton Street Line</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prospect_Park_(Brooklyn)" title="Prospect Park (Brooklyn)">Prospect Park</a> is a public park in central Brooklyn encompassing 585 acres (2.37&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-parkstat_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parkstat-83">[83]</a></sup> The park was designed by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Law_Olmsted" title="Frederick Law Olmsted">Frederick Law Olmsted</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calvert_Vaux" title="Calvert Vaux">Calvert Vaux</a>, who created Manhattan's <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>. Attractions include the Long Meadow, a 90-acre (36&#160;ha) meadow, the Picnic House, which houses offices and a hall that can accommodate parties with up to 175 guests; <a href="/wiki/Litchfield_Villa" title="Litchfield Villa">Litchfield Villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Park_Zoo" title="Prospect Park Zoo">Prospect Park Zoo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boathouse_on_the_Lullwater_of_the_Lake_in_Prospect_Park" title="Boathouse on the Lullwater of the Lake in Prospect Park">Boathouse</a>, housing a visitors center and the first urban <a href="/wiki/National_Audubon_Society" title="National Audubon Society">Audubon Center</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-auduboncenter_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auduboncenter-84">[84]</a></sup> Brooklyn's only lake, covering 60 acres (24&#160;ha); the Prospect Park Bandshell that hosts free outdoor concerts in the summertime; and various sports and fitness activities including seven baseball fields. Prospect Park hosts a popular annual Halloween Parade.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Brooklyn" title="Sports in Brooklyn">Sports in Brooklyn</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg/250px-Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg/375px-Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg/500px-Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barclays_Center_Rain_Night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Pacific Park, Brooklyn">Pacific Park</a> within <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Heights,_Brooklyn" title="Prospect Heights, Brooklyn">Prospect Heights</a>, is Brooklyn's premier sports venue.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brooklyn's major professional sports teams are the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Brooklyn Nets</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_York_Islanders" title="New York Islanders">New York Islanders</a>. The Nets and Islanders moved into the borough in 2012 and 2015, respectively, and both play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a> in Prospect Heights. Previously, the Nets had played in <a href="/wiki/Uniondale,_New_York" title="Uniondale, New York">Uniondale, New York</a> and in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, while the Islanders had played in Uniondale since their inception.</p>
<p>Brooklyn also has a storied sports history. It has been home to many famous sports figures such as <a href="/wiki/Joe_Paterno" title="Joe Paterno">Joe Paterno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vince_Lombardi" title="Vince Lombardi">Vince Lombardi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Torre" title="Joe Torre">Joe Torre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vitas_Gerulaitis" title="Vitas Gerulaitis">Vitas Gerulaitis</a>. Basketball legend <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan" title="Michael Jordan">Michael Jordan</a> was born in Brooklyn though he grew up in <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_North_Carolina" title="Wilmington, North Carolina">Wilmington, North Carolina</a>.</p>
<p>In the earliest days of organized baseball, Brooklyn teams dominated the new game. The second recorded game of baseball was played near what is today <a href="/wiki/Fort_Greene_Park" title="Fort Greene Park">Fort Greene Park</a> on October 24, 1845. Brooklyn’s <a href="/wiki/Excelsior_of_Brooklyn" title="Excelsior of Brooklyn">Excelsiors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Atlantics" title="Brooklyn Atlantics">Atlantics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eckford_of_Brooklyn" title="Eckford of Brooklyn">Eckfords</a> were the leading teams from the mid-1850s through the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>, and there were dozens of local teams with neighborhood league play, such as at <a href="/wiki/Mapleton_Park,_Brooklyn,_NY" class="mw-redirect" title="Mapleton Park, Brooklyn, NY">Mapleton Oval</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BrooklynBallParks.com_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BrooklynBallParks.com-85">[85]</a></sup> During this "Brooklyn era", baseball evolved into the modern game: the first <a href="/wiki/Fastball" title="Fastball">fastball</a>, first <a href="/wiki/Changeup" title="Changeup">changeup</a>, first <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>, first <a href="/wiki/Triple_play" title="Triple play">triple play</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Creighton" title="Jim Creighton">first pro baseball player</a>, first <a href="/wiki/Union_Grounds" title="Union Grounds">enclosed ballpark</a>, first <a href="/wiki/Baseball_scorekeeping" title="Baseball scorekeeping">scorecard</a>, first known African-American team, first black championship game, first road trip, first gambling scandal, and first eight pennant winners were all in or from Brooklyn.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brooklyn's most famous historical team, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a>, named for "trolley dodgers" played at <a href="/wiki/Ebbets_Field" title="Ebbets Field">Ebbets Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In 1947 <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> was hired by the Dodgers as the first African-American player in Major League Baseball in the modern era. In 1955, the Dodgers, perennial National League pennant winners, won the only <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> for Brooklyn against their rival <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. The event was marked by mass euphoria and celebrations. Just two years later, the Dodgers moved to Los Angeles. <a href="/wiki/Walter_O%27Malley" title="Walter O'Malley">Walter O'Malley</a>, the team's owner at the time, is still vilified, even by Brooklynites too young to remember the Dodgers as Brooklyn's ball club.</p>
<p>After a 43-year hiatus, professional baseball returned to the borough in 2001 with the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Cyclones" title="Brooklyn Cyclones">Brooklyn Cyclones</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor league baseball">minor league</a> team that plays in <a href="/wiki/MCU_Park" title="MCU Park">MCU Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Coney_Island" title="Coney Island">Coney Island</a>. They are an affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>.</p>
<p>Brooklyn once had a <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> team named the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Lions" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Lions">Brooklyn Lions</a> in the 1920s, who played at <a href="/wiki/Ebbets_Field" title="Ebbets Field">Ebbets Field</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_New_York_City" title="Transportation in New York City">Transportation in New York City</a></div>
<p>About 57 percent of all households in Brooklyn were households without <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>. The citywide rate is 55 percent in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg/250px-Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg/375px-Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg/500px-Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coney_Island-Stillwell_Avenue_Terminus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Coney_Island_%E2%80%93_Stillwell_Avenue" class="mw-redirect" title="Coney Island – Stillwell Avenue">Coney Island&#160;– Stillwell Avenue</a> subway station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brooklyn features extensive <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transit</a>. Eighteen <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a> services, including the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Avenue_Shuttle" title="Franklin Avenue Shuttle">Franklin Avenue Shuttle</a>, traverse the borough. Approximately 92.8% of Brooklyn residents traveling to Manhattan use the subway, despite the fact that some neighborhoods like <a href="/wiki/Flatlands,_Brooklyn" title="Flatlands, Brooklyn">Flatlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marine_Park" title="Marine Park">Marine Park</a> are poorly served by subway service. Major stations, out of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_City_Subway_stations_in_Brooklyn" title="List of New York City Subway stations in Brooklyn">170 currently in Brooklyn</a>, include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Avenue_%E2%80%93_Barclays_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Avenue – Barclays Center">Atlantic Avenue&#160;– Barclays Center</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Broadway_Junction_(New_York_City_Subway)" title="Broadway Junction (New York City Subway)">Broadway Junction</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DeKalb_Avenue_(BMT_Fourth_Avenue_Line)" title="DeKalb Avenue (BMT Fourth Avenue Line)">DeKalb Avenue</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jay_Street_%E2%80%93_MetroTech" class="mw-redirect" title="Jay Street – MetroTech">Jay Street&#160;– MetroTech</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coney_Island_%E2%80%93_Stillwell_Avenue" class="mw-redirect" title="Coney Island – Stillwell Avenue">Coney Island&#160;– Stillwell Avenue</a><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Proposed New York City Subway lines never built include a line along Nostrand or Utica Avenues to Marine Park,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> as well as a subway line to <a href="/wiki/Spring_Creek,_Brooklyn" title="Spring Creek, Brooklyn">Spring Creek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brooklyn was once served by <a href="/wiki/List_of_streetcar_lines_in_Brooklyn" title="List of streetcar lines in Brooklyn">an extensive network of streetcars</a>, many of which were replaced by <a href="/wiki/List_of_bus_routes_in_Brooklyn" title="List of bus routes in Brooklyn">the public bus network that covers the entire borough</a>. There is also daily express bus service into Manhattan. New York's famous yellow cabs also provide transportation in Brooklyn, although they are less numerous in the borough. There are three commuter rail stations in Brooklyn: <a href="/wiki/East_New_York_(LIRR_station)" title="East New York (LIRR station)">East New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nostrand_Avenue_(LIRR_station)" title="Nostrand Avenue (LIRR station)">Nostrand Avenue</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Terminal" title="Atlantic Terminal">Atlantic Terminal</a>, the terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Branch" title="Atlantic Branch">Atlantic Branch</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Rail_Road" title="Long Island Rail Road">Long Island Rail Road</a>. The terminal is located near the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Avenue_%E2%80%93_Barclays_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Avenue – Barclays Center">Atlantic Avenue&#160;– Barclays Center</a> subway station, with ten connecting subway services.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Streetcar" class="mw-redirect" title="Streetcar">streetcar</a> line <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Queens_Connector" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Queens Connector">connecting Brooklyn with Queens</a> was proposed by the city in February 2016, with the planned timeline calling for service to begin around 2024.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roadways">Roadways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Roadways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_streets" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn streets">Brooklyn streets</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_lettered_Brooklyn_avenues" title="List of lettered Brooklyn avenues">List of lettered Brooklyn avenues</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Eastern_Parkway_Looking_towards_Museum_Eugene_Wemlinger_ca._1903-_1910_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/View_of_Eastern_Parkway_Looking_towards_Museum_Eugene_Wemlinger_ca._1903-_1910_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg/400px-View_of_Eastern_Parkway_Looking_towards_Museum_Eugene_Wemlinger_ca._1903-_1910_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg" width="400" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/View_of_Eastern_Parkway_Looking_towards_Museum_Eugene_Wemlinger_ca._1903-_1910_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg/600px-View_of_Eastern_Parkway_Looking_towards_Museum_Eugene_Wemlinger_ca._1903-_1910_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/View_of_Eastern_Parkway_Looking_towards_Museum_Eugene_Wemlinger_ca._1903-_1910_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg/800px-View_of_Eastern_Parkway_Looking_towards_Museum_Eugene_Wemlinger_ca._1903-_1910_Brooklyn_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1115" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbcaption">
