<a href="/wiki/Williamsburg_Bridge" title="Williamsburg Bridge">Williamsburg Bridge</a>, as seen from <a href="/wiki/Wallabout_Bay" title="Wallabout Bay">Wallabout Bay</a> with <a href="/wiki/Greenpoint,_Brooklyn" title="Greenpoint, Brooklyn">Greenpoint</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_City" title="Long Island City">Long Island City</a> in background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The great majority of <a href="/wiki/Limited-access_road" title="Limited-access road">limited-access expressways and parkways</a> are located in the western and southern sections of Brooklyn. These include the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn-Queens_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn-Queens Expressway">Brooklyn-Queens Expressway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gowanus_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Gowanus Expressway">Gowanus Expressway</a> (which is part of the Brooklyn-Queens Expressway), the <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Prospect Expressway">Prospect Expressway</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Route_27" title="New York State Route 27">New York State Route 27</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Belt_Parkway" title="Belt Parkway">Belt Parkway</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson_Parkway" title="Jackie Robinson Parkway">Jackie Robinson Parkway</a> (formerly the Interborough Parkway). Planned expressways that were never built include the Bushwick Expressway, an extension of <a href="/wiki/I-78" class="mw-redirect" title="I-78">I-78</a><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and the Cross-Brooklyn Expressway, I-878.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Major thoroughfares include <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Avenue_(New_York_City)" title="Atlantic Avenue (New York City)">Atlantic Avenue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Avenue_(Brooklyn)" title="Fourth Avenue (Brooklyn)">Fourth Avenue</a>, 86th Street, <a href="/wiki/Kings_Highway_(Brooklyn)" title="Kings Highway (Brooklyn)">Kings Highway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Parkway_(Brooklyn)" title="Bay Parkway (Brooklyn)">Bay Parkway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Parkway_(Brooklyn)" title="Ocean Parkway (Brooklyn)">Ocean Parkway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Parkway" title="Eastern Parkway">Eastern Parkway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linden_Boulevard" title="Linden Boulevard">Linden Boulevard</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGuinness_Boulevard" title="McGuinness Boulevard">McGuinness Boulevard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flatbush_Avenue" title="Flatbush Avenue">Flatbush Avenue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Avenue_(Brooklyn)" title="Pennsylvania Avenue (Brooklyn)">Pennsylvania Avenue</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nostrand_Avenue" title="Nostrand Avenue">Nostrand Avenue</a>.</p>
<p>Much of Brooklyn has only named streets, but <a href="/wiki/Park_Slope" title="Park Slope">Park Slope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Ridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay Ridge">Bay Ridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Sunset Park, Brooklyn">Sunset Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bensonhurst" class="mw-redirect" title="Bensonhurst">Bensonhurst</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Borough_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Borough Park, Brooklyn">Borough Park</a> and the other western sections have <a href="/wiki/List_of_numbered_Brooklyn_streets" title="List of numbered Brooklyn streets">numbered streets</a> running approximately northwest to southeast, and numbered avenues going approximately northeast to southwest. East of Dahill Road, lettered avenues (like Avenue M) run east and west, and numbered streets have the prefix "East". South of Avenue O, related numbered streets west of Dahill Road use the "West" designation. This set of numbered streets ranges from West 37th Street to East 108 Street, and the avenues range from A-Z with names substituted for some of them in some neighborhoods (notably Albemarle, Beverley, Cortelyou, Dorchester, Ditmas, Foster, Farragut, Glenwood, Quentin). Numbered streets prefixed by "North" and "South" in Williamsburg, and "Bay", "Beach", "Brighton", "Plumb", "Paerdegat" or "Flatlands" along the southern and southwestern waterfront are loosely based on the old grids of the original towns of Kings County that eventually consolidated to form Brooklyn. These names often reflect the bodies of water or beaches around them, such as <a href="/wiki/Plumb_Beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Plumb Beach">Plumb Beach</a> or <a href="/wiki/Paerdegat_Basin" title="Paerdegat Basin">Paerdegat Basin</a>.</p>
<p>Brooklyn is connected to Manhattan by three bridges, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">Brooklyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Bridge" title="Manhattan Bridge">Manhattan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg_Bridge" title="Williamsburg Bridge">Williamsburg</a> bridges; a vehicular tunnel, the <a href="/wiki/Hugh_L._Carey_Tunnel" class="mw-redirect" title="Hugh L. Carey Tunnel">Hugh L. Carey Tunnel</a> (formerly the Brooklyn-Battery Tunnel); and several subway tunnels. The <a href="/wiki/Verrazano-Narrows_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Verrazano-Narrows Bridge">Verrazano-Narrows Bridge</a> links Brooklyn with the more suburban borough of <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a>. Though much of its border is on land, Brooklyn shares several water crossings with <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Kosciuszko_Bridge_(New_York_City)" title="Kosciuszko Bridge (New York City)">Kosciuszko Bridge</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn-Queens_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn-Queens Expressway">Brooklyn-Queens Expressway</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Pulaski_Bridge" title="Pulaski Bridge">Pulaski Bridge</a>, and the JJ Byrne Memorial Bridge, all of which carry traffic over <a href="/wiki/Newtown_Creek" title="Newtown Creek">Newtown Creek</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Parkway_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Parkway Bridge">Marine Parkway Bridge</a> connecting Brooklyn to the <a href="/wiki/Rockaway_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Rockaway Peninsula">Rockaway Peninsula</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">Waterways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Waterways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Brooklyn was long a major shipping port, especially at the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Army_Terminal" title="Brooklyn Army Terminal">Brooklyn Army Terminal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Sunset Park, Brooklyn">Sunset Park</a>. Most container ship cargo operations have shifted to the New Jersey side of New York Harbor, while the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Cruise_Terminal" title="Brooklyn Cruise Terminal">Brooklyn Cruise Terminal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Red_Hook,_Brooklyn" title="Red Hook, Brooklyn">Red Hook</a> is a focal point for New York's growing cruise industry. The <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Mary_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Mary 2">Queen Mary 2</a></i>, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_world%27s_largest_cruise_ships" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the world's largest cruise ships">world's largest ocean liners</a>, was designed specifically to fit under the <a href="/wiki/Verrazano-Narrows_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Verrazano-Narrows Bridge">Verrazano-Narrows Bridge</a>, the longest suspension bridge in the United States. She makes regular ports of call at the Red Hook terminal on her transatlantic crossings from <a href="/wiki/Southampton,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Southampton, England">Southampton, England</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/NY_Waterway" title="NY Waterway">NY Waterway</a> offers commuter services from the western shore of Brooklyn to points in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_City" title="Long Island City">Long Island City</a>, as well as tours and charters. <a href="/wiki/SeaStreak" title="SeaStreak">SeaStreak</a> also offers weekday ferry service between the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Army_Terminal" title="Brooklyn Army Terminal">Brooklyn Army Terminal</a> and the Manhattan ferry slips at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pier_11&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pier 11 (page does not exist)">Pier 11</a> downtown and <a href="/wiki/East_34th_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="East 34th Street">East 34th Street</a> in midtown. A <a href="/wiki/Cross-Harbor_Rail_Tunnel" title="Cross-Harbor Rail Tunnel">Cross-Harbor Rail Tunnel</a>, originally proposed in the 1920s as a core project for the then new <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Authority of New York">Port Authority of New York</a> is again being studied and discussed as a way to ease freight movements across a large swath of the metropolitan area.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1508px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG" class="image" title="Manhattan Bridge seen from Brooklyn Bridge Park."><img alt="Manhattan Bridge" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG/1500px-Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG" width="1500" height="224" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG/2250px-Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG/3000px-Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG 2x" data-file-width="12416" data-file-height="1856" /></a></div>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manhattan_Bridge_Panorama.JPG" title="File:Manhattan Bridge Panorama.JPG"></a></div>
Manhattan Bridge seen from <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge_Park" title="Brooklyn Bridge Park">Brooklyn Bridge Park</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_New_York_City" title="Education in New York City">Education in New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_New_York_City" title="List of high schools in New York City">List of high schools in New York City</a></div>
<p>Education in Brooklyn is provided by a vast number of public and private institutions. Public schools in the borough are managed by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Education" title="New York City Department of Education">New York City Department of Education</a>, the largest public school system.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Technical_High_School" title="Brooklyn Technical High School">Brooklyn Technical High School</a> (commonly called Brooklyn Tech), a New York City public high school, is the largest specialized high school for science, mathematics, and technology in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Brooklyn Tech opened in 1922. Brooklyn Tech is located across the street from <a href="/wiki/Fort_Greene_Park" title="Fort Greene Park">Fort Greene Park</a>. This high school was built from 1930 to 1933 at a cost of about $6,000,000 and is 12 stories high. It covers about half of a city block.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Brooklyn Tech is noted for its famous alumni<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> (including two Nobel Laureates), its academics, and the large number of graduates attending prestigious universities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_colleges">Public colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Public colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_College" title="Brooklyn College">Brooklyn College</a> is a senior college of the <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">City University of New York</a>, and was the first public coeducational <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts_college" title="Liberal arts college">liberal arts college</a> in New York City. The College ranked in the top 10 nationally for the second consecutive year in <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" class="mw-redirect" title="Princeton Review">Princeton Review</a>’s 2006 guidebook, <i>America’s Best Value Colleges</i>. Many of its students are first and second generation Americans.</p>
<p>Founded in 1970, <a href="/wiki/Medgar_Evers_College" title="Medgar Evers College">Medgar Evers College</a> is a senior college of the <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">City University of New York</a>, with a mission to develop and maintain high quality, professional, career-oriented undergraduate degree programs in the context of a liberal arts education. The College offers programs both at the baccalaureate and associate degree levels, as well as Adult and Continuing Education classes for Central Brooklyn residents, corporations, government agencies, and community organizations. Medgar Evers College is a few blocks east of <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Park_(Brooklyn)" title="Prospect Park (Brooklyn)">Prospect Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Crown_Heights,_Brooklyn" title="Crown Heights, Brooklyn">Crown Heights</a>.</p>
<p>CUNY's <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_College_of_Technology" title="New York City College of Technology">New York City College of Technology</a> (City Tech) of The City University of New York (CUNY) (Downtown Brooklyn/Brooklyn Heights) is the largest public college of technology in New York State and a national model for technological education. Established in 1946, City Tech can trace its roots to 1881 when the Technical Schools of the Metropolitan Museum of Art were renamed the New York Trade School. That institution—which became the Voorhees Technical Institute many decades later—was soon a model for the development of technical and vocational schools worldwide. In 1971, Voorhees was incorporated into City Tech.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/SUNY_Downstate_College_of_Medicine" title="SUNY Downstate College of Medicine">SUNY Downstate College of Medicine</a>, originally founded as the Long Island College Hospital in 1860, is the oldest hospital-based medical school in the United States. The Medical Center comprises the College of Medicine, College of Health Related Professions, College of Nursing, School of Public Health, School of Graduate Studies, and University Hospital of Brooklyn. The Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Furchgott" title="Robert F. Furchgott">Robert F. Furchgott</a> was a member of its faculty. Half of the Medical Center's students are minorities or immigrants. The College of Medicine has the highest percentage of minority students of any medical school in New York State.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_colleges">Private colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Private colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg/220px-Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="346" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg/330px-Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg/440px-Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1693" data-file-height="2666" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Law_School_Fell_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Law_School" title="Brooklyn Law School">Brooklyn Law School</a>'s 1994 <a href="/wiki/New_Classical_Architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="New Classical Architecture">new classical</a> "Fell Hall" tower, by architect <a href="/wiki/Robert_A._M._Stern" title="Robert A. M. Stern">Robert A. M. Stern</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Law_School" title="Brooklyn Law School">Brooklyn Law School</a> was founded in 1901 and is notable for its diverse student body. Women and African Americans were enrolled in 1909. According to the Leiter Report, a compendium of law school rankings published by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Leiter" title="Brian Leiter">Brian Leiter</a>, Brooklyn Law School places 31st nationally for quality of students.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Long_Island_University" title="Long Island University">Long Island University</a> is a private university headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Brookville,_New_York" title="Brookville, New York">Brookville</a> on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, with a campus in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Brooklyn" title="Downtown Brooklyn">Downtown Brooklyn</a> with 6,417 undergraduate students. The Brooklyn campus has strong science and medical technology programs, at the graduate and undergraduate levels.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pratt_Institute" title="Pratt Institute">Pratt Institute</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Hill,_Brooklyn" title="Clinton Hill, Brooklyn">Clinton Hill</a>, is a private college founded in 1887 with programs in engineering, architecture, and the arts. Some buildings in the school's Brooklyn campus are <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Landmarks_Preservation_Commission" title="New York City Landmarks Preservation Commission">official landmarks</a>. Pratt has over 4700 students, with most at its Brooklyn campus. Graduate programs include library and information science, architecture, and urban planning. Undergraduate programs include architecture, construction management, writing, critical and visual studies, industrial design and fine arts, totaling over 25 programs in all.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg/220px-Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg/330px-Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg/440px-Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1558" data-file-height="1182" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wunsch_building_among_MetroTech.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/New_York_University_Tandon_School_of_Engineering" title="New York University Tandon School of Engineering">NYU Tandon</a> Wunsch Building</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_Tandon_School_of_Engineering" title="New York University Tandon School of Engineering">New York University Tandon School of Engineering</a>, the United States' second oldest private <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">institute of technology</a>, founded in 1854, has its main campus in Downtown's <a href="/wiki/MetroTech_Center" title="MetroTech Center">MetroTech Center</a>, a commercial, civic and educational redevelopment project of which it was a key sponsor. NYU-Tandon is one of the 18 schools and colleges that comprise <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> (NYU).<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/St._Francis_College" title="St. Francis College">St. Francis College</a> is a Catholic college located in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Heights" title="Brooklyn Heights">Brooklyn Heights</a> and was founded in 1859 by Franciscan friars. Today, there are over 2,400 students attending the small liberal arts college. St. Francis is considered by the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> as one of the more diverse colleges, and was ranked one of the best baccalaureate colleges by both <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine and <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimesDiversity_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimesDiversity-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes.com_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes.com-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brooklyn also has smaller liberal arts institutions, such as <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_College_(New_York)" title="St. Joseph's College (New York)">Saint Joseph's College</a> in Clinton Hill and <a href="/wiki/Boricua_College" title="Boricua College">Boricua College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Brooklyn" title="Williamsburg, Brooklyn">Williamsburg</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_colleges">Community colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Community colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kingsborough_Community_College" title="Kingsborough Community College">Kingsborough Community College</a> is a junior college in the <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">City University of New York</a> system, located in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Beach,_Brooklyn" title="Manhattan Beach, Brooklyn">Manhattan Beach</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brooklyn_Public_Library">Brooklyn Public Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Brooklyn Public Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG/220px-Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG/330px-Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG/440px-Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Public_Library_by_DS.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Central Library at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Army_Plaza" title="Grand Army Plaza">Grand Army Plaza</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As an independent system, separate from the New York and Queens public library systems, the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Public_Library" title="Brooklyn Public Library">Brooklyn Public Library</a><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> offers thousands of public programs, millions of books, and use of more than 850 free Internet-accessible computers. It also has books and periodicals in all the major languages spoken in Brooklyn, including English, Russian, Chinese, Spanish, Hebrew, and <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Krey%C3%B2l" class="mw-redirect" title="Haitian Kreyòl">Haitian&#160;Kreyòl</a>, as well as French, Yiddish, Hindi, Bengali, Polish, Italian, and Arabic. The Central Library is a landmarked building facing <a href="/wiki/Grand_Army_Plaza" title="Grand Army Plaza">Grand Army Plaza</a>.</p>
<p>There are 58 library branches, placing one within a half mile of each Brooklyn resident. In addition to its specialized Business Library in Brooklyn Heights, the Library is preparing to construct its new Visual &amp; Performing Arts Library (VPA) in the BAM Cultural District, which will focus on the link between new and emerging arts and technology and house traditional and digital collections. It will provide access and training to arts applications and technologies not widely available to the public. The collections will include the subjects of art, theater, dance, music, film, photography and architecture. A special archive will house the records and history of Brooklyn's arts communities.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hospitals_and_healthcare">Hospitals and healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Hospitals and healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_New_York_City#Brooklyn" title="List of hospitals in New York City">List of hospitals in New York City §&#160;Brooklyn</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brookdale_University_Hospital_and_Medical_Center" title="Brookdale University Hospital and Medical Center">Brookdale University Hospital and Medical Center</a> <sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Medical_Society_of_the_County_of_Kings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Medical Society of the County of Kings (page does not exist)">Medical Society of the County of Kings</a>, Inc. (founded 1822): its mission is "to foster progress in the science and art of medicine and to promote, preserve and enforce the highest of standards of ethical and proficient medical care".<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Published_1950.E2.80.93present">Published 1950–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brooklyn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Published 1950–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<ul>
<li>Curran, Winifred. "Gentrification and the nature of work: exploring the links in Williamsburg, Brooklyn." <i>Environment And Planning A.</i> 36 (2004): 1243-1258.</li>
<li>Curran, Winifred. "'From the Frying Pan to the Oven': Gentrification and the Experience of Industrial Displacement in Williamsburg, Brooklyn." <i>Urban Studies</i> (2007) 44#8 pp: 1427-1440.</li>

<li>Livingston, E. H. <i>President Lincoln's Third Largest City: Brooklyn and The Civil War</i> (1994)</li>

<li>Warf, Barney. "The reconstruction of social ecology and neighborhood change in Brooklyn." <i>Environment and Planning D</i> (1990) 8#1 pp: 73-96.</li>
<li>Wellman, Judith. <i>Brooklyn's Promised Land: The Free Black Community of Weeksville, New York</i> (2014)</li>
